GT: -c0*sqrt(A) - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.12072*sqrt(A) - 0.12072*A*exp(-0.06862*t) + 0.8537*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three basis functions:
1. `sqrt(A)` — a square root term
2. `A*exp(c*t)` — exponential decay in t multiplied by A
3. `sin(log(A + 1))` — sine of logarithm

Key observation: `sin(log(A+1))` is a very specific transcendental function. None of the candidates contain `sin()` at all. Let me verify this by checking every candidate carefully.

Looking through all 50 candidates, I see the following types of basis functions used:
- `A*exp(c*t)` — present in many candidates ✓
- `log(A*c + 1)` — present in many candidates
- `exp(A*c)` — exponential in A
- `A/(A*c + 1)^2` — rational functions
- `A/(A + c)` — rational functions
- `sqrt(A)` — only in Candidate 34
- `Abs(A)` — in several candidates
- `A^2` — in some candidates
- `log(A*c+1)/(A*c+1)` — rational-log combinations

**Critical issue:** The GT contains `sin(log(A + 1))`, which is a fundamentally different basis function from `log(A + 1)`. No finite linear combination of `log(A+c)`, `exp(A*c)`, `A/(A+c)^n`, polynomial terms, etc., can exactly reproduce `sin(log(A+1))` for all A ≥ 0. These are linearly independent function classes.

Since `sin(log(A+1))` cannot be expressed as any combination of the basis functions present in any of the 50 candidates (logarithms, exponentials, rational functions, polynomials, square roots), **none of the candidates can match the GT**.

Let me double-check Candidate 34 since it has `sqrt(A)`:
`sqrt(A)*c0 + A*c1*exp(A*c2) + A*c3/(A*c4 + 1)**2 + A*c5*exp(c6*t) + c7*log(A*c8 + 1)`

Even though it has `sqrt(A)` and `A*exp(c*t)`, it lacks `sin(log(A+1))` and instead has `log(A*c+1)`, `exp(A*c)`, and rational terms. These cannot combine to form `sin(log(A+1))`.
